Summary of Manufacturing AI Transformation (AX) Trend Analysis

This summary analyzes 10 recently published key technical documents to present core trends, opportunities, and challenges in manufacturing AI transformation.

The most prominent trend is process virtualization and system integration centered around 'Digital Twin' and 'Digital Thread'. This aims to resolve problems in advance by simulating processes (virtual commissioning) in a virtual environment, and to secure transparency across the entire value chain by connecting distributed data from systems like PLM, MES, and ERP.

Additionally, 'Predictive Maintenance (PdM)' and 'Predictive Quality Control (PQC)' have established themselves as the most practical AI application areas. Through vibration data analysis, automated vision inspection, and other methods, they predict equipment failures and quality defects in advance, minimizing downtime and maximizing yield.

Recently, the emergence of 'Generative AI' and 'manufacturing-specific AI models' is noteworthy. These technologies are opening up opportunities for 'Hyper-automation', going beyond existing automation, such as the intelligentization of collaborative robots, automated quotation, and the development of AI models trainable even with small amounts of data.

However, for successful AI adoption, the complexity of data integration and solving 'Small-Data' learning problems specific to the field are key challenges. Therefore, in the short term, it is necessary to focus on areas where clear ROI can be expected, such as predictive maintenance, and in the long term, a phased approach is required to establish data governance and move towards an enterprise-wide AI-based decision-making system.

The Hadrian case presents an operating model that simultaneously reduces lead time and variability by connecting quoting, programming, machining, and inspection with a digital thread, as part of a vertical integration strategy of 'designing the factory like a product.' It suggests using 4x utilization rate, 10x productivity, and 30-day onboarding as benchmarks, and managing spindle utilization, touch time, and FPY as core KPIs. From an implementation perspective, standardization and automation are expanded through an end-to-end software backbone connecting ERP, MES, CAM, and CMM; parametric automated quoting; tool/jig standardization; CMM data-driven closed-loop quality; and digital work instructions/guided programming. With a CAPEX+software combination, scaling is possible for high-demand environments such as defense/aerospace. However, to secure supply chain resilience and performance sustainability, initial investment, part mix complexity, security/data governance, and change management risks must be pre-designed.

The Hadrian case demonstrates a smart factory model that achieved a 4-fold increase in utilization rate, a 10-fold increase in labor productivity, and 30-day training by integrating quotation, programming, machining, and inspection into a single software flow. Key learning points include vertical integration based on a digital thread, automated quotation and closed-loop quality, tool and jig standardization, and rapid expansion through role-based digital work instructions. It provides practical implications for shortening lead times in defense and aerospace supply chains and for reindustrialization strategies, and can be deployed as an operational system centered on KPIs (spindle utilization, touch time, FPY). However, phased implementation considering initial CAPEX, data and security regulations, and change management is desirable.

By connecting PLM, MES, ERP, and QMS in real-time with an AI-based integrated platform to establish a single digital thread, it is possible to trace the root causes of scrap, quality issues, and process variations, and shorten NPI/process approval lead times. In the expansion of metal additive manufacturing (especially DED), AI toolpath adaptation combining real-time sensing and simulation, including bead height, is expected to reduce cycle time, homogenize heat input, and improve yield and reproducibility. Implement an 8-12 week pilot with a KPI board (FPY, scrap rate, cycle time, etc.) and correlation analysis based on standardized cause codes, applying a closed-loop for alarm/parameter guidance. In aerospace and defense environments, establish security governance with Zero Trust, role-based access, encryption, and ITAR/EAR compliance.

This AI wave, unlike IoT/Industry 4.0, accelerates a shift from a cost-reduction focus to a value-creation focus across factories and supply chains, due to data fluidity, mature edge-cloud infrastructure, and industry-specific models. Neuromeka's AI-based situational awareness, real-time collision avoidance, sensorless collision detection/impedance control, and direct teaching shorten collaborative robots' setup and teaching times, simultaneously increasing safety and utilization rate, making them immediately applicable to variable processes such as high-mix low-volume production and welding. The 10kg-class lightweight welding robot roadmap, vertical integration (robot foundry) strategy, and large-scale reference with POSCO accelerate adoption in small and medium-sized enterprises (SMEs), shipbuilding, and post-processing sites by securing cost, lead time, and quality consistency, and through layout flexibility. Upon deployment, quantifying setup/teaching time, cycle time, FPY, and safety indicators in a pilot, alongside concurrently ensuring ISO/TS safety compliance and MES/QA linkage, can maximize the TCO improvement effect.

It states that NC AI has been selected as the national representative AI to develop a sovereign AI foundation model specialized in industrial data. ë³¸ ì—°êµ¬ëŠ” ì‹¤í—˜ì‹¤/ì˜¨ë¼ì¸ ë°ì´í„°ì™€ ì‹¤ì œ ì œì¡° í˜„ì¥ ê°„ ì„±ëŠ¥ ê²©ì°¨ë¥¼ í™•ì¸í•˜ë©°, ë³µì¡í•œ ëŒ€í˜• ëª¨ë¸ë³´ë‹¤ ê³µì •Â·ì¡°ëª…Â·ì¬ì§ˆ ë“± í˜„ì¥ ë§¥ë½ì— ë§ì¶˜ ë„ë©”ì¸ íŠ¹í™”Â·ê²½ëŸ‰ ëª¨ë¸ì˜ ê· í˜• ì„¤ê³„ê°€ ì¤‘ìš”í•¨ì„ ê°•ì¡°í•©ë‹ˆë‹¤. ì‹¤ë¬´ì ìœ¼ë¡œëŠ” ë‹¤ì–‘í•œ ì¡°ê±´ì˜ í˜„ì¥ ë°ì´í„°ì…‹ êµ¬ì¶•ê³¼ ë„ë©”ì¸ ì ì‘/ì¦ê°•, ì‘ì—…Â·ì¥ë¹„ ì¡°ê±´ì„ í¬í•¨í•œ ë§¥ë½ ë©”íƒ€ë°ì´í„°Â·í”„ë¡¬í”„íŠ¸ ì„¤ê³„, ëŒ€í˜• ëª¨ë¸â†’ê²½ëŸ‰ ì—£ì§€ ëª¨ë¸ ì§€ì‹ ì¦ë¥˜ë¥¼ í†µí•´ ë¼ì¸ ì¹´ë©”ë¼ ê¸°ë°˜ì˜ ì‹¤ì‹œê°„ í’ˆì§ˆ ì ê²€ê³¼ ì•ˆì „ ê²½ë³´ë¥¼ ë™ì‹œì— êµ¬í˜„í•  ìˆ˜ ìˆìŠµë‹ˆë‹¤. ë˜í•œ KPI(ì •ë°€ë„/ì¬í˜„ìœ¨, ì˜¤ê²½ë³´ìœ¨, ê²€ì‚¬ ì‚¬ì´í´ íƒ€ì„, ì¬ì‘ì—…ë¥ , ê·¼ì ‘ì‚¬ê³  ê°ì†Œìœ¨)ë¥¼ MLOpsë¡œ ëª¨ë‹ˆí„°ë§í•´ ì„±ëŠ¥ ë“œë¦¬í”„íŠ¸ë¥¼ ê´€ë¦¬í•˜ì‹­ì‹œì˜¤. This study identifies the performance gap between laboratory/online data and actual manufacturing sites, and emphasizes that, rather than complex large models, a balanced design of domain-specific and lightweight models tailored to the field context, such as process, lighting, and material, is crucial. Practically, by building field datasets under various conditions, domain adaptation/augmentation, designing contextual metadata and prompts including work and equipment conditions, and distilling knowledge from large models to lightweight edge models, real-time quality inspection and safety alarms can be simultaneously implemented based on line cameras. Additionally, use MLOps to monitor KPIs (precision/recall, false alarm rate, inspection cycle time, rework rate, near-miss reduction rate) to manage performance drift.

A study by the University of Notre Dame confirmed that while AI can evaluate welding quality, its performance is lower in actual field welding compared to images curated online. This emphasizes the importance of 'field data acquisition and labeling' and 'domain adaptation/distillation'. Furthermore, context-specific prompts are effective for performance improvement, and since large models are not always the answer, a lightweight, domain-specific model strategy reflecting field constraints is necessary. Manufacturing sites can simultaneously enhance quality inspection accuracy and worker safety through real-data-centric learning/validation, prompt templating, distillation-based edge deployment, and drift monitoring.

By overlaying 'Control Tower' type agentic AI across manufacturing ERP/EAM/APS/MES to connect events in a closed loop from subscription, recommendation, approval, to execution, ERP can be transformed from a system of record into a System of Action, enabling the automation of planning, exception handling, procurement, inventory, and maintenance scheduling even amidst labor shortages. Generative AI interprets unstructured documents such as SOPs, specifications, and contracts, and agentic AI performs event-based decision-making and orchestration. Secure tangible ROI within 6 to 12 months through phased pilots equipped with governance (including master data/history/demand signal reliability, roles, approval limits, and monitoring), KPIs (such as planning lead time, inventory turnover, OTD), and Human-in-the-Loop.

The core of the article is that agentic AI can transform ERP/EAM/supply chain systems from 'record'-centric to 'action'-centric, achieving quick ROI in a labor-scarce environment. It proposes a division of roles where generative AI is suited for document and knowledge processing, while agentic AI is appropriate for control tower-type decision-making and execution orchestration. However, the fact that data quality determines success or failure, coupled with the prospect that a significant number of agentic AI projects might be canceled by 2027, suggests the importance of governance, including phased pilots, KPI-based verification, Human-in-the-Loop, approval limits, and audit trails. Practically, a strategy that starts with low-risk and quick-impact areas such as purchase exception handling, inventory redeployment, and MRO work order scheduling, and then gradually expands the scope of automation, is effective.

Applying AI-based computer vision AOI/AXI in-line enables real-time detection of solder and component misplacement, and trace/via defects, improving FPY and DPMO, and reducing rework and escape defects. Through closed-loop integration with SPI, chip mounter, and reflow, process variations can be automatically compensated. Standardization of optics/illumination and a data strategy centered on 'golden board â€“ defect classification â€“ annotation standardization â€“ synthetic/augmented data,' when combined with edge inference, X-ray integration (multimodal), and predictive analytics, simultaneously achieves minimal tact time impact and expanded inspection coverage. Implementation should proceed in PoC â†’ Pilot â†’ Line Expansion stages, and should include MES/trace linkage, MLOps (versioning, retraining, validation) for addressing model drift, a yield improvement recovery plan for initial CAPEX, and on-site training/change management.

This article presents a direction for quality management that utilizes AI computer vision to detect defects inline and correct processes with real-time feedback in PCB processes. Key values are improved yield (FPY) and DPMO, reduced rework/scrap, and mitigated human dependency. As a recent trend, the multimodal combination of deep learning and X-ray, along with the application of predictive quality, is emphasized. For successful adoption, a data strategy including golden board, defect classification, and annotation standards, along with standardization of optical settings, MLOps to address model drift, MES/trace linkage, and phased deployment from PoC to pilot to expansion are necessary. While initial investment and skilled personnel requirements exist, ROI achievement is possible by minimizing tact time impact (through edge inference) and expanding coverage.

KPIëŠ” ìë™í™”ìœ¨ë¿ ì•„ë‹ˆë¼ ë¶ˆëŸ‰ë¥ Â·ì‚¬ê³ ìœ¨Â·ì¹¨í•´ ì´ë²¤íŠ¸Â·ì—ë„ˆì§€ ì§‘ì•½ë„ë¥¼ í•¨ê»˜ ê´€ë¦¬í•´ ì „ì²´ ìµœì í™”ë¥¼ ë‹¬ì„±í•´ì•¼ í•©ë‹ˆë‹¤. Dark factories improve efficiency and reduce costs by implementing full automation through AI, robots, and IoT, but preparation for job displacement, OT/IoT cybersecurity, environmental risks such as energy and e-waste, and algorithm bias is essential. The optimal solution is an augmented intelligence operating model, applying a human-in-the-loop approach where AI handles detection, prediction, and recommendation, and humans make final decisions in the context of quality, safety, and regulation, while also strengthening security through data governance/bias monitoring, network segmentation, patching, and visibility, and simultaneously implementing a reskilling roadmap. KPIs should manage not only the automation rate but also the defect rate, accident rate, breach events, and energy intensity together to achieve overall optimization.

The article points out that while dark factories offer advantages in terms of efficiency and cost, they are accompanied by job displacement, cybersecurity risks, and environmental impacts. AI and computer vision quality inspection in smart production lines realizes human-machine collaboration of Industry 5.0, increasing inspection consistency and speed, and enabling augmented operations where operators focus on final decision-making and exception handling (Refer to BMW case study). Given the premise of AI manufacturing investment bubbles and geopolitical risks, incorporate demand fluctuations, tariffs/export regulations, and chip/accelerator supply and demand scenarios into the risk management system, and absorb supply chain shocks through edge-cloud hybrid and accelerator diversification. We present an on-site implementation pattern that integrates AI cameras with industrial panel PCs (HMI/IPC, WinGP) to detect safety regulation violations in real-time, such as solo work, unequipped PPE, and hazardous zone intrusion. Daegu City offers support for AI adoption and demonstration (up to KRW 130-150 million), consulting (KRW 8-15 million), and platform services (model recommendation, simulation, chatbot) to small and medium-sized manufacturing enterprises (SMEs) focused on machine elements and material parts. A 30% cash matching contribution is mandatory. Within the application period (August 11 - August 22, 5 PM), it is effective to prepare project proposals and data samples, design a Proof of Concept (PoC) by standardizing equipment, process, and quality logs, setting Key Performance Indicators (KPIs) such as defect rate, OEE, and cycle time, and defining priority tasks (vision inspection, predictive maintenance, process simulation, on-site chatbot), and then verify generalization performance through cross-validation.

This media roundup presents two directions for Manufacturing AI Transformation. Firstly, the automation of dangerous and high-difficulty tasks is becoming a reality with humanoid-based physical AI. This article presents an execution path for expanding AI use cases directly linked to factory operations and supply chain performance (predictive maintenance, process anomaly/quality inspection, demand/inventory forecasting) from PoC to expansion, using a value-based roadmap. By managing energy and utility KPIs (electricity, steam, solvent, OEE/energy intensity/scrap) and leveraging EMS/APC/RTO linked with process data, short-term costs and emissions can be reduced. Furthermore, it enhances resilience through supplier diversification, inventory and lead time visualization, and multimodal/alternative route scenario planning (in a high-mix, low-volume environment, modular equipment and recipe-centric MES are concurrently used), and provides a practical framework applicable across manufacturing.

The article summarizes key trends in chemical manufacturing (AI, sustainability, supply chain resilience, bio-based materials, demand for specialty chemicals) and presents actionable directions for immediate application in manufacturing sites. In the short term, strategies to improve costs and OEE through predictive maintenance, AI quality inspection, and process and energy optimization are effective. In the medium term, strategies to enhance responsiveness to high-mix, low-volume production through conversion to bio-based raw materials, modular production, and MES/APS integration are valid. From a supply chain perspective, external shocks can be absorbed through diversified sourcing, multimodal logistics, and scenario-based planning.

í†µí•© ì¸ì‚¬ì´íŠ¸:Consolidated Insight:

The priority from a manufacturing AX perspective is to combine AI-based circular design (durability, repairability, modularity) with DPP/traceability (IoT+cloud) to implement multi-lifecycle operation (recovery â€“ repair/remanufacturing â€“ re-introduction), computer vision-based sorting, and reverse logistics optimization; the pilot should be deployed in the order of predictive maintenance â†’ reverse logistics/remanufacturing â†’ quality/waste sorting, and automate EPR compliance and recycled raw material verification through ecosystem partner collaboration and standard integration. By combining RAG and Transformer fine-tuning in manufacturing HRI, field manuals, SOPs, maintenance history, and sensor data like acoustics can be searched and interpreted in real-time to enhance worker/robot decision-making and adaptive learning. The recommended architecture consists of edge inference LLM/multimodal models, on-premise vector DB (integrated with MES/CMMS/PLM), and safety guardrails, and can be immediately applied for purposes such as changeover guides, proposals for FPY degradation causes, and summaries of predictive maintenance alarms and recommendations for inspection procedures. Upon implementation, low-latency (~200ms) design, data curation, chunking, domain embedding, human-in-the-loop, and performance/safety metrics should be used to control hallucination, outdated knowledge, and security risks.
ìš”ì•½:Summary:
ê¸°ì‚¬ì˜ í•µì‹¬ì€ RAGì™€ íŠ¸ëœìŠ¤í¬ë¨¸ ë¯¸ì„¸ì¡°ì •ì„ ì œì¡° ë¡œë³´í‹±ìŠ¤/HRIì— ì ìš©í•´ ë™ì  í™˜ê²½ì—ì„œ ì‹¤ì‹œê°„ ì˜ì‚¬ê²°ì •ê³¼ ì§€ì‹ ê²€ìƒ‰ì„ ê°•í™”í•˜ìëŠ” ì œì•ˆì…ë‹ˆë‹¤. ë§¤ë‰´ì–¼Â·SOPÂ·ìœ ì§€ë³´ìˆ˜ ì´ë ¥ ë“± ë‚´ë¶€ ì§€ì‹ì„ ë²¡í„°DBë¡œ ê´€ë¦¬í•˜ê³ , ì—£ì§€ LLMì´ ì´ë¥¼ ê²€ìƒ‰Â·ìš”ì•½í•´ ì‘ì—…ìì™€ ë¡œë´‡ì— êµ¬ì²´ì  ê¶Œê³ ë¥¼ ì œê³µí•˜ë©´ êµì²´/ì…‹ì—…, í’ˆì§ˆ íŠ¸ëŸ¬ë¸”ìŠˆíŒ…, ì˜ˆì§€ë³´ì „, ì•ˆì „ ëŒ€ì‘ì— ì§ì ‘ì ìœ¼ë¡œ ê¸°ì—¬í•  ìˆ˜ ìˆìŠµë‹ˆë‹¤. ë©€í‹°ëª¨ë‹¬(ê°€ì²­/ë¹„ê°€ì²­ ìŒí–¥ ë“±) ê²°í•©ìœ¼ë¡œ ì´ìƒê²€ì¶œ ì„¤ëª…ê°€ëŠ¥ì„±ë„ í–¥ìƒë©ë‹ˆë‹¤. ì‹¤ë¬´ì ìœ¼ë¡œëŠ” ì˜¨í”„ë ˆë¯¸ìŠ¤ ì•„í‚¤í…ì²˜, ë°ì´í„° ê±°ë²„ë„ŒìŠ¤, ì§€ì—°ì‹œê°„ ê´€ë¦¬, íœ´ë¨¼-ì¸-ë”-ë£¨í”„, ì‹ ë¢°ë„/ì¶œì²˜ í‘œê¸°, ì•ˆì „ ê°€ë“œë ˆì¼ ë„ì…ì´ ê´€ê±´ì´ë©°, ì„±ê³µ ì§€í‘œë¡œ MTTR, FPY, ê¶Œê³  ìˆ˜ìš©ë¥ , í—ˆìœ„ê²½ë³´ìœ¨ì„ ì¶”ì²œí•©ë‹ˆë‹¤. The core of the article is a proposal to enhance real-time decision-making and knowledge retrieval in dynamic environments by applying RAG and Transformer fine-tuning to manufacturing robotics/HRI. By managing internal knowledge such as manuals, SOPs, and maintenance history as a vector database, and having an edge LLM search and summarize this information to provide specific recommendations to workers and robots, it can directly contribute to replacement/setup, quality troubleshooting, predictive maintenance, and safety responses. Combining multimodal data (such as audible/inaudible acoustics) also enhances the explainability of anomaly detection. Practically, the key factors are the adoption of on-premise architecture, data governance, latency management, human-in-the-loop, reliability/source indication, and safety guardrails, and MTTR, FPY, recommendation acceptance rate, and false alarm rate are recommended as success metrics.

This article proposes a direction to accelerate Time-to-Value (TTV) by overcoming the high costs, lengthy implementation times, and limited use cases that hinder the widespread adoption of robot automation. This is achieved through 'closed-loop AI + low-code' robotics software, which shortens programming time, automatically incorporates quality and safety via vision/sensor feedback, and adapts to variable environments. Effective implementation points for manufacturing sites include: accelerating the learning cycle with narrow Proof-of-Concepts (PoCs) after defining TTV metrics, expanding field engineer participation through low-code, designing vision/sensor feedback loops, enabling MES/PLC/CMMS event-driven integration, and pre-defining AI guardrails and approval workflows.

For practical application, it is effective to clearly define TTV metrics, create fast learning cycles with small-scale PoCs, and design governance that includes MES/PLC integration and approval procedures (Guardrails). IoWT wearables serve as a core AX layer connecting people, equipment, and processes in real-time, accelerating on-site decision-making such as safety interlocks, early detection of quality anomalies, and AR work guides by combining worker status and process context through multi-modal sensor fusion and edge AI. For operational expansion, key factors include interoperability of heterogeneous devices, equipment, and MES/CMMS/SCADA, privacy- and security-centric data governance, and TCO reduction through energy harvesting/low-power design. Practically, start PoCs from high-risk cells, specify baseline delays and alarm policies, link alarm-work order automation, and track performance with KPIs such as TRIR, downtime, and throughput.

This workshop CFP strategically outlines the utilization of wearable IoT in manufacturing sites. SMRs are modular nuclear power plants that convert on-site construction to factory manufacturing. Their core lies in ultra-precision mass production capabilities, including design-manufacturing integration (digital thread/MBSE), nuclear-grade quality systems (ASME, ISO 19443, NQA-1), and automated NDT/robotic/laser welding. Based on its large nuclear power plant and heavy industry base (e.g., Doosan Enerbility, HD Hyundai), Korea should establish an 'SMR manufacturing foundry' to secure a leading position in the 22% growth market, and, along with strategic investment zones, specialized safety certification, and tax support, it must strengthen power resilience with PPA/CHP and microgrid models for data centers and smart factories.

The increasing power demand in the AI era is directly linked to power resilience strategies (SMR + Microgrid, PPA) at manufacturing sites. In terms of execution, design-manufacturing integration based on Digital Thread/MBSE, nuclear-grade quality and traceability systems, and the utilization of regulatory sandboxes and tax incentives determine success.

AI sensor feedback-based closed-loop robotic sheet metal/composite forming completes parts 'within a few hours' without physical molds, accelerating design-manufacturing iterations and providing time and cost competitiveness in prototyping, bridge production, and low-volume high-mix manufacturing. In fields such as aerospace and defense, where frequent design changes and high security requirements are common, a customer on-site co-location (on-site deployment) model can simultaneously secure quality and delivery times, and the integration of digital workflows encompassing metals/composites minimizes re-tooling and enhances process agility. Practically, you should prioritize reviewing the internalization of closed-loop sensing and adaptive control, the economic re-evaluation of converting tooling costs to digital toolpaths, time/cost benchmarking through pilots, and the establishment of robotic path planning, sensor fusion, and QA data capabilities.

Machina Labs is expanding a manufacturing method that leverages AI sensors and robots to perform die-less sheet metal forming and digitally process the production of composite molds and parts. By producing multiple parts within hours, it reduces costs and lead times compared to traditional processes, and is pursuing on-site deployment models in the aerospace and defense (USAF/NASA) sectors. For manufacturing professionals, key implications include the economics in low-volume, high-mix / bridge production, acceleration of design-to-manufacturing iteration, customer on-site co-location strategies, and the necessity of adopting closed-loop sensing and adaptive control.

It proposes a practical approach that, in manufacturing sites, links RPA with MES/ERP/SCADA and CMMS to automate repetitive and rule-based tasks such as issuing work orders, inputting quality/regulatory records, and ordering materials and spare parts. By combining with AI, it extends to processing unstructured data like document recognition and ticket classification, and even to predictive maintenance triggers (work order generation, parts reservation, notifications). As a pilot (8-12 weeks), by selecting high-frequency, high-volume, and clearly defined rule-based processes and verifying the effects with KPIs (cycle time, error/exception rate, compliance SLA), and by gradually expanding with API-centric integration and CoE/governance, ROI, cost reduction, accuracy, scalability, and compliance improvement can be expected within 6-12 months. However, since the automation potential varies depending on process complexity, risks such as vendor lock-in and model drift must be managed at the design stage.

The halt of Tesla Dojo and the Samsung AI chip partnership suggest that high-compute workloads such as large-scale vision, robotics, and quality analysis should be portfolioed from a 'build vs. buy' perspective, and CAPEX/OPEX should be managed based on TCO, including power, cooling, yield, and lead time. A 4 billion atom-level AI simulation can simultaneously optimize energy, cost, and emissions through material/process digital twins, and 97% accurate edge vision can be immediately applied to safety and quality monitoring, including pedestrian and forklift collision prevention and hazardous area intrusion detection. Practical Recommendation: Systematically manage 12-24 month compute demand forecasting and chip/cloud procurement scenarios, joint roadmaps with key partners, and metrics for edge vision pilots including MTBF, False Alarm Rate, and Intervention Time.

Manufacturing has been the most frequent target of cyberattacks for four consecutive years (approx. 26%), and amidst an average data breach cost of $4.44 million and increasing IP theft, oversharing of regulated data and trade secrets is a core risk when integrated with GenAI/LLM, enterprise search, and collaboration tools. From a practical standpoint, it is effective to identify and organize the oversharing of core assets such as PLM/CAD, process documents, and supply chain contracts from the perspective of accounts, links, and external sharing (minimum privilege, expiration, owner re-evaluation), prevent recurrence through source system labeling, DLP, and automated permissions, and simultaneously implement AI usage policies (prohibited data categories, prompt detection/blocking, log and anomaly monitoring) along with partner account segregation and export control (e.g., ITAR) compliance.

Murata's mass production of 'stretchable substrates' with up to 60% elongation opens new process and quality dimensions for flexible electronics manufacturing in wearable, medical, and automotive electronics. From a manufacturing AX perspective, key elements include detecting defects under deformation using in-line vision/AI, early failure prediction and recipe optimization through thermal-mechanical FEA-based digital twin and durability test data learning, and establishing MES/traceability for the R2R printing-bonding-curing integrated line. Furthermore, preempting the standardization of medical regulations (QMS/UDI), biocompatible material tracking, and reliability metrics (resistance change rate, adhesion, bending radius) will enable securing a competitive advantage in the growing healthcare and vehicle HMI markets.

Murata's mass production plan for stretchable substrates (up to 60% elongation) will promote process innovation in wearable and medical device manufacturing. Manufacturers must predict the thermo-mechanical behavior of elastomer-metal circuits with digital twins, early detect defects under stretching using in-line AI inspection, and close-loop optimize recipes based on repetitive stretch durability metrics. Key implementation points include medical regulations and traceability requirements, the adoption of non-traditional packaging/bonding technologies (ACF, conductive adhesives), and Roll-to-Roll (R2R) process integration. Aiming at the growing market (projected $838 billion by 2034), it is worthwhile to prepare for differentiation through pilot-to-mass production transition, OEM co-design, and reliability standardization.

In an environment where bilateral and regional trade orders are strengthening due to the weakening of the WTO, the manufacturing industry must redesign its localization and friendshoring portfolios for production, procurement, and R&D by mapping tariffs, non-tariff barriers, rules of origin, digital trade regulations, and incentives specific to each industry for key markets such as China, EU, India, and Central/South America, and strengthen its capabilities for external negotiations and policy response. From an AX perspective, it is effective to establish AI scenario planning that digitalizes trade and policy risks (tariff and CBAM simulations), automated HS code classification, origin tracking, and export control/certification compliance, and dashboards that link country-specific market accessibility/regulatory complexity indicators with order and production plans, and to provide digital compliance tools and training to partners to enhance supply chain compliance and delivery times. Internally, competitiveness must be maintained amidst the spread of protectionism by streamlining redundant approvals/regulations and utilizing regulatory sandboxes to speed up investment and pilot projects and ensure policy consistency.

With the weakening of the WTO system, Korean manufacturing needs industry-specific trade strategies tailored to a trade order centered on bilateral and regional agreements. Korean manufacturers, amidst the US-China competitive landscape, must realign their positioning by adopting a dual-track manufacturing AX strategy that separates core IP and equipment to the US-allied ecosystem, and sales and services within China to local operations. Throughout AX investment and operations, internalize China risks and execute KPI-based derisking for dependencies on parts/materials and customs delays, concurrently pursuing China+1/reshoring, and redesigning lead time and inventory policies. Simultaneously, enhance regulatory responsiveness through stack and cloud redundancy considering data localization and by establishing a 'China Desk' (policy intelligence and specialized translation). In areas of strength such as semiconductors, equipment, smart manufacturing software, and medical AI, pursue partnerships but clearly define IP boundaries.

Gyeongsangbuk-do's K-Scientist Matching Day is an attempt to link AI infrastructure (local data centers) and next-generation energy (SMRs, hydrogen production linked to high-temperature processes) as key regional projects. For the manufacturing industry, energy costs, carbon reduction potential, and accessibility to smart factory computing infrastructure can be improved. In particular, the promotion of SMR regulatory free zones is an institutional opportunity to test process heat integration, safety protocols, and maintenance standards. It is an effective strategy for companies to proactively prepare for heat demand mapping, TEA, participation in regulatory special zone consortia, and edge-core data architecture design to secure tangible results and incentives in initial pilot projects.

Epicor's Cognitive ERP transforms ERP from 'record-keeping' to an 'execution' platform based on real-time analysis and prediction, and improves operational efficiency and supplier collaboration through integration with SourceDay (automation and exception management for the entire purchase order lifecycle) and Sovos (standardization of global e-invoicing and tax compliance). Manufacturers should start with procurement and tax, which offer high ROI, and set KPI baselines such as on-time delivery rate, change order processing time, and supplier response rate. They should also pilot with key suppliers and tune alerts/workflows, and secure the consistency of material/customer master data and change history, as well as supplier adoption rate, through templates, portal training, and SLAs, to establish a closed loop of exception detection â†’ action â†’ feedback.

Epicor has realized its intelligent ERP vision by strengthening procurement automation and tax compliance in Kinetic ERP through partnerships with SourceDay and Sovos. Manufacturers can proactively manage delivery risks by standardizing procurement exception management and supplier collaboration, and reduce regional regulatory risks and manual labor by embedding electronic reporting requirements. For short-term actions, establishing procurement KPI baselines, piloting with key suppliers, designing notifications and workflows, data quality refinement, and supplier onboarding are recommended.
